<h1 class="firstHeading mw-first-heading" id="firstHeading"><span class="mw-page-title-main">Military</span></h1>
<div class="vector-body" id="bodyContent">
<div class="noprint" id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>

<div id="contentSub2"></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:141113-A-QS211-509_-_Soldiers_of_the_1st_Brigade_Combat_Team,_1st_Cavalry_Division,_and_2nd_Cavalry_Regiment_participate_in_the_closing_ceremony_for_Iron_Sword_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1345" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="184" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/141113-A-QS211-509_-_Soldiers_of_the_1st_Brigade_Combat_Team%2C_1st_Cavalry_Division%2C_and_2nd_Cavalry_Regiment_participate_in_the_closing_ceremony_for_Iron_Sword_2014.jpg/280px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/141113-A-QS211-509_-_Soldiers_of_the_1st_Brigade_Combat_Team%2C_1st_Cavalry_Division%2C_and_2nd_Cavalry_Regiment_participate_in_the_closing_ceremony_for_Iron_Sword_2014.jpg/420px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/141113-A-QS211-509_-_Soldiers_of_the_1st_Brigade_Combat_Team%2C_1st_Cavalry_Division%2C_and_2nd_Cavalry_Regiment_participate_in_the_closing_ceremony_for_Iron_Sword_2014.jpg/560px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="280"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:141113-A-QS211-509_-_Soldiers_of_the_1st_Brigade_Combat_Team,_1st_Cavalry_Division,_and_2nd_Cavalry_Regiment_participate_in_the_closing_ceremony_for_Iron_Sword_2014.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> military ceremony, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pabrade" title="Pabrade">Pabrade</a>, Lithuania in November 2014</div></div></div>
<p>A <b>military</b>, also known collectively as <b>armed forces</b>, is a heavily armed, highly organized force primarily intended for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Warfare" title="Warfare">warfare</a>. It is typically authorized and maintained by a <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a>, with its members identifiable by their distinct <a href="/wiki/Military_uniform" title="Military uniform">military uniform</a>. It may consist of one or more <a href="/wiki/Military_branch" title="Military branch">military branches</a> such as an <a href="/wiki/Army" title="Army">army</a>, <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">navy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_force" title="Air force">air force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Space_force" title="Space force">space force</a>, <a href="/wiki/Marines" title="Marines">marines</a>, or <a href="/wiki/Coast_guard" title="Coast guard">coast guard</a>. The main task of the military is usually defined as defence of the state and its interests against external armed threats.
</p><p>In broad usage, the terms <i>armed forces</i> and <i>military</i> are often treated as synonymous, although in technical usage a distinction is sometimes made in which a country's armed forces may include both its military and other <a href="/wiki/Paramilitary" title="Paramilitary">paramilitary</a> forces. There are various forms of <a href="/wiki/Irregular_military" title="Irregular military">irregular military</a> forces, not belonging to a recognized state; though they share many attributes with regular military forces, they are less often referred to as simply <i>military</i>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:352px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Countries_by_soldier_count.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="263" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Countries_by_soldier_count.svg/350px-Countries_by_soldier_count.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Countries_by_soldier_count.svg/525px-Countries_by_soldier_count.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Countries_by_soldier_count.svg/700px-Countries_by_soldier_count.svg.png 2x" width="350"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Countries_by_soldier_count.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Countries by number of active soldiers (2009)</div></div></div>
<p>A nation's military may function as a discrete social <a href="/wiki/Subculture" title="Subculture">subculture</a>, with dedicated infrastructure such as military housing, schools, utilities, <a href="/wiki/Logistics" title="Logistics">logistics</a>, hospitals, legal services, food production, finance, and banking services. Beyond warfare, the military may be employed in additional sanctioned and non-sanctioned functions within the state, including internal security threats, <a href="/wiki/Population_control" title="Population control">population control</a>, the promotion of a <a href="/wiki/Political_agenda" title="Political agenda">political agenda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emergency_service" title="Emergency service">emergency services</a> and reconstruction, protecting <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corporate" title="Corporate">corporate</a> economic interests, social ceremonies and national honour guards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1">[1]</a></sup>
</p><p>The profession of <a href="/wiki/Soldier" title="Soldier">soldiering</a> as part of a military is older than <a href="/wiki/Recorded_history" title="Recorded history">recorded history</a> itself.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> Some of the most enduring images of  <a href="/wiki/Classical_antiquity" title="Classical antiquity">classical antiquity</a> portray the power and feats of its military <a href="/wiki/Leadership" title="Leadership">leaders</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kadesh" title="Battle of Kadesh">Battle of Kadesh</a> in 1274 BC was one of the defining points of Pharaoh <a href="/wiki/Ramesses_II" title="Ramesses II">Ramses II</a>'s reign, and his monuments commemorate it in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bas-relief" title="Bas-relief">bas-relief</a>. A thousand years later, the first <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_China" title="Emperor of China">emperor of unified China</a>, <a href="/wiki/Qin_Shi_Huang" title="Qin Shi Huang">Qin Shi Huang</a>, was so determined to impress the gods with his military might that he had himself buried with an army of  <a href="/wiki/Terracotta_Army" title="Terracotta Army">terracotta soldiers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-3">[3]</a></sup>
The  <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Rome" title="Ancient Rome">Romans</a> paid considerable attention to military matters, leaving to posterity many <a href="/wiki/Treatise" title="Treatise">treatises</a> and writings on the subject, as well as many lavishly carved <a href="/wiki/Triumphal_arch" title="Triumphal arch">triumphal arches</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victory_column" title="Victory column">victory columns</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology_and_definitions">Etymology and definitions</span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A0%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BA_%E2%84%96_2_%D0%BA_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%8C%D0%B5_%C2%AB%D0%95%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%BD%D1%8B%C2%BB._%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D1%8D%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%A1%D1%8B%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0_(%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3,_1911-1915).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="938" data-file-width="1061" decoding="async" height="194" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/%D0%A0%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BA_%E2%84%96_2_%D0%BA_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%8C%D0%B5_%C2%AB%D0%95%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%BD%D1%8B%C2%BB._%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D1%8D%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%A1%D1%8B%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0_%28%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3%2C_1911-1915%29.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/%D0%A0%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BA_%E2%84%96_2_%D0%BA_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%8C%D0%B5_%C2%AB%D0%95%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%BD%D1%8B%C2%BB._%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D1%8D%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%A1%D1%8B%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0_%28%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3%2C_1911-1915%29.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/19/%D0%A0%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BA_%E2%84%96_2_%D0%BA_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%8C%D0%B5_%C2%AB%D0%95%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%BD%D1%8B%C2%BB._%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D1%8D%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%A1%D1%8B%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0_%28%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3%2C_1911-1915%29.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:%D0%A0%D0%B8%D1%81%D1%83%D0%BD%D0%BE%D0%BA_%E2%84%96_2_%D0%BA_%D1%81%D1%82%D0%B0%D1%82%D1%8C%D0%B5_%C2%AB%D0%95%D0%B3%D0%B8%D0%BF%D0%B5%D1%82%D1%81%D0%BA%D0%B8%D0%B5_%D0%B2%D0%BE%D0%B9%D0%BD%D1%8B%C2%BB._%D0%92%D0%BE%D0%B5%D0%BD%D0%BD%D0%B0%D1%8F_%D1%8D%D0%BD%D1%86%D0%B8%D0%BA%D0%BB%D0%BE%D0%BF%D0%B5%D0%B4%D0%B8%D1%8F_%D0%A1%D1%8B%D1%82%D0%B8%D0%BD%D0%B0_(%D0%A1%D0%B0%D0%BD%D0%BA%D1%82-%D0%9F%D0%B5%D1%82%D0%B5%D1%80%D0%B1%D1%83%D1%80%D0%B3,_1911-1915).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Depiction of <a href="/wiki/Military_of_ancient_Egypt" title="Military of ancient Egypt">ancient Egyptian military</a> formation</div></div></div>
<p>The first recorded use of the word military in English, spelled <span title="Middle English (1100-1500)-language text"><i lang="enm">militarie</i></span>, was in 1582.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OED_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-OED-4">[4]</a></sup> It comes from the Latin <i>militaris</i> (from Latin <i>miles</i>, meaning "soldier") through French, but is of uncertain etymology, one suggestion being derived from <i>*mil-it-</i> – going in a body or mass.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup>
</p><p>As a noun, the military usually refers generally to a country's armed forces, or sometimes, more specifically, to the senior officers who command them.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OED_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-OED-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Webster_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Webster-7">[7]</a></sup> In general, it refers to the physicality of armed forces, their <a href="/wiki/Military_personnel" title="Military personnel">personnel</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_technology" title="Military technology">equipment</a>, and the physical area which they occupy.
</p><p>As an adjective, military originally referred only to soldiers and soldiering, but it soon broadened to apply to land forces in general, and anything to do with their profession.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OED_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-OED-4">[4]</a></sup> The names of both the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Military_Academy,_Woolwich" title="Royal Military Academy, Woolwich">Royal Military Academy</a> (1741) and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Military_Academy" title="United States Military Academy">United States Military Academy</a> (1802) reflect this. However, at about the time of the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, 'military' began to be used in reference to armed forces as a whole, such as '<a href="/wiki/Military_service" title="Military service">military service</a>', '<a href="/wiki/Military_intelligence" title="Military intelligence">military intelligence</a>', and '<a href="/wiki/Military_history" title="Military history">military history</a>'. As such, it now connotes any activity performed by armed force personnel.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OED_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-OED-4">[4]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_history" title="Military history">Military history</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Riace_bronzes_-_Statue_A-_Ancient_Greek_warrior.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2370" data-file-width="1444" decoding="async" height="279" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Riace_bronzes_-_Statue_A-_Ancient_Greek_warrior.jpg/170px-Riace_bronzes_-_Statue_A-_Ancient_Greek_warrior.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Riace_bronzes_-_Statue_A-_Ancient_Greek_warrior.jpg/255px-Riace_bronzes_-_Statue_A-_Ancient_Greek_warrior.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/98/Riace_bronzes_-_Statue_A-_Ancient_Greek_warrior.jpg/340px-Riace_bronzes_-_Statue_A-_Ancient_Greek_warrior.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Riace_bronzes_-_Statue_A-_Ancient_Greek_warrior.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An Ancient Greek warrior demonstrates the effectiveness of <a href="/wiki/Power_training#Historical_examples_of_power-type_training" title="Power training">contemporary physical training</a> regimes. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Riace_Bronzes" title="Riace Bronzes">Riace Bronzes</a>, c.450 BC</div></div></div>
<p>Military history is often considered to be the history of all conflicts, not just the history of the state militaries. It differs somewhat from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/History_of_war" title="History of war">history of war</a>, with military history focusing on the people and institutions of war-making, while the history of war focuses on the evolution of war itself in the face of changing technology, governments, and geography.
</p><p>Military history has a number of facets. One main facet is to learn from past accomplishments and mistakes, so as to more effectively wage war in the future. Another is to create a sense of <a href="/wiki/Military_tradition" title="Military tradition">military tradition</a>, which is used to create cohesive military forces. Still, another may be to learn to prevent wars more effectively. Human knowledge about the military is largely based on both recorded and <a href="/wiki/Oral_history" title="Oral history">oral history</a> of military conflicts (war), their participating <a href="/wiki/Army" title="Army">armies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">navies</a> and, more recently, <a href="/wiki/Air_force" title="Air force">air forces</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Organization">Organization</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Military_organization" title="Military organization">Military organization</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GCCMAP_2019.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="6000" data-file-width="11100" decoding="async" height="162" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/78/GCCMAP_2019.png/300px-GCCMAP_2019.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/78/GCCMAP_2019.png/450px-GCCMAP_2019.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/7/78/GCCMAP_2019.png/600px-GCCMAP_2019.png 2x" width="300"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GCCMAP_2019.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An example of military command; a map of the United States' Unified Combatant Command's area of responsibility.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Personnel_and_units">Personnel and units</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_personnel" title="Military personnel">Military personnel</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Military_reserve" title="Military reserve">Military reserve</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_service" title="Military service">Military service</a></div>
<p>Despite the growing importance of <a href="/wiki/Military_technology" title="Military technology">military technology</a>, military activity depends above all on people. For example, in 2000 the British Army declared: "Man is still the first weapon of war."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rank_and_role">Rank and role</span></h4>
<p>The military organization is characterized by a strict <a href="/wiki/Command_hierarchy" title="Command hierarchy">command hierarchy</a> divided by <a href="/wiki/Military_rank" title="Military rank">military rank</a>, with ranks normally grouped (in descending order of authority) as <a href="/wiki/Officer_(armed_forces)" title="Officer (armed forces)">officers</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Colonel" title="Colonel">Colonel</a>), <a href="/wiki/Non-commissioned_officer" title="Non-commissioned officer">non-commissioned officers</a> (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Sergeant" title="Sergeant">Sergeant</a>), and personnel at the lowest rank (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Private_(rank)" title="Private (rank)">Private Soldier</a>). While senior officers make strategic decisions, subordinated military personnel (<a href="/wiki/Soldier" title="Soldier">soldiers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sailor" title="Sailor">sailors</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Marine_(military)" title="Marine (military)">marines</a>, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Airmen" title="Airmen">airmen</a>) fulfil them. Although rank titles vary by <a href="/wiki/Military_branch" title="Military branch">military branch</a> and country, the rank hierarchy is common to all state armed forces worldwide.
</p><p>In addition to their rank, personnel occupy one of many trade roles, which are often grouped according to the nature of the role's military tasks on combat operations: <a href="/wiki/Combat" title="Combat">combat</a> roles (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Infantry" title="Infantry">infantry</a>), <a href="/wiki/Combat_support" title="Combat support">combat support</a> roles (e.g. <a href="/wiki/Combat_engineer" title="Combat engineer">combat engineers</a>), and <a href="/wiki/Combat_service_support" title="Combat service support">combat service support</a> roles (e.g. logistical support).
</p><p>In the past, the armed forces of some Communist states, such as the Soviet Union, China and Albania, have attempted to abolish military ranks, but they were later reintroduced due to operational difficulties relating to <a href="/wiki/Command_and_control" title="Command and control">command and control</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Recruitment">Recruitment</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_recruitment" title="Military recruitment">Military recruitment</a></div>
<p>Personnel may be <a href="/wiki/Military_recruitment" title="Military recruitment">recruited</a> or <a href="/wiki/Conscription" title="Conscription">conscripted</a>, depending on the system chosen by the state. Most military personnel are males; the minority proportion of female personnel varies internationally (approximately 3% in India,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> 10% in the UK,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> 13% in Sweden,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> 16% in the US,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> and 27% in South Africa<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup>). While two-thirds of states now recruit or conscript only adults, as of 2017 50 states still relied partly on children under the age of 18 (usually aged 16 or 17) to staff their armed forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:2_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-:2-15">[15]</a></sup>
</p><p>Whereas recruits who join as <a href="/wiki/Officer_(armed_forces)" title="Officer (armed forces)">officers</a> tend to be <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Upwardly_mobile" title="Upwardly mobile">upwardly-mobile</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_16-0"><a href="#cite_note-:4-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> most enlisted personnel have a childhood background of relative <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Socio-economic_gap" title="Socio-economic gap">socio-economic deprivation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:0_18-0"><a href="#cite_note-:0-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup> For example, after the US suspended conscription in 1973, "the military disproportionately attracted African American men, men from lower-status socioeconomic backgrounds, men who had been in nonacademic high school programs, and men whose high school grades tended to be low".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:4_16-1"><a href="#cite_note-:4-16">[16]</a></sup> However, a study released in 2020 on the socio-economic backgrounds of U.S. Armed Forces personnel suggests that they are at parity or slightly higher than the civilian population with respect to socio-economic indicators such as parental income, parental wealth and cognitive abilities. The study found that technological, tactical, operational and doctrinal changes have led to a change in the demand for personnel. Furthermore, the study suggests that the most disadvantaged socio-economic groups are less likely to meet the requirements of the modern U.S. military.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Obligations">Obligations</span></h4>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_recruitment" title="Military recruitment">Military recruitment</a></div>
<p>The obligations of military employment are many. Full-time military employment normally requires a minimum period of service of several years; between two and six years is typical of armed forces in Australia, the UK and the US, for example, depending on role, branch, and rank.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:522_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-:522-23">[23]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:622_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-:622-24">[24]</a></sup> Some armed forces allow a short <a href="/wiki/Military_discharge" title="Military discharge">discharge</a> window, normally during training, when recruits may leave the armed force as of right.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:72_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-:72-25">[25]</a></sup> Alternatively, part-time military employment, known as <a href="/wiki/Military_reserve_force" title="Military reserve force">reserve service</a>, allows a recruit to maintain a civilian job while training under military discipline at weekends; he or she may be called out to <a href="/wiki/Military_operation" title="Military operation">deploy on operations</a> to supplement the full-time personnel complement. After leaving the armed forces, recruits may remain liable for compulsory return to full-time military employment in order to train or <a href="/wiki/Military_operation" title="Military operation">deploy on operations</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:72_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-:72-25">[25]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:622_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-:622-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_Law" title="Military Law">Military law</a> introduces offences not recognised by civilian courts, such as <a href="/wiki/Desertion" title="Desertion">absence without leave (AWOL)</a>, desertion, political acts, <a href="/wiki/Malingering" title="Malingering">malingering</a>, behaving disrespectfully, and disobedience (see, for example, <a href="/wiki/Offences_against_military_law_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Offences against military law in the United Kingdom">offences against military law in the United Kingdom</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:82_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-:82-26">[26]</a></sup> Penalties range from a summary <a href="/wiki/Reprimand" title="Reprimand">reprimand</a> to imprisonment for several years following a <a href="/wiki/Court-martial" title="Court-martial">court martial</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:82_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-:82-26">[26]</a></sup> Certain fundamental rights are also restricted or suspended, including the freedom of association (e.g. union organizing) and freedom of speech (speaking to the media).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:82_26-2"><a href="#cite_note-:82-26">[26]</a></sup> Military personnel in some countries have a right of <a href="/wiki/Conscientious_objector" title="Conscientious objector">conscientious objection</a> if they believe an order is immoral or unlawful, or cannot in good conscience carry it out.
</p><p>Personnel may be posted to bases in their home country or overseas, according to operational need, and may be deployed from those bases on <a href="/wiki/Military_exercise" title="Military exercise">exercises</a> or <a href="/wiki/Military_operation" title="Military operation">operations</a> anywhere in the world. During peacetime, when military personnel are generally stationed in <a href="/wiki/Garrison" title="Garrison">garrisons</a> or other permanent military facilities, they mostly conduct administrative tasks, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_training" title="Military training">training</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_education" title="Military education">education</a> activities, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maintenance,_repair_and_operations" title="Maintenance, repair and operations">technology maintenance</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_recruitment" title="Military recruitment">and recruitment</a>.
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Training">Training</span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USRAK_soldiers_attend_Finnish_army%27s_cold_weather_training_150110-A-WX507-585.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="1836" decoding="async" height="302" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/USRAK_soldiers_attend_Finnish_army%27s_cold_weather_training_150110-A-WX507-585.jpg/170px-USRAK_soldiers_attend_Finnish_army%27s_cold_weather_training_150110-A-WX507-585.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/USRAK_soldiers_attend_Finnish_army%27s_cold_weather_training_150110-A-WX507-585.jpg/255px-USRAK_soldiers_attend_Finnish_army%27s_cold_weather_training_150110-A-WX507-585.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/USRAK_soldiers_attend_Finnish_army%27s_cold_weather_training_150110-A-WX507-585.jpg/340px-USRAK_soldiers_attend_Finnish_army%27s_cold_weather_training_150110-A-WX507-585.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USRAK_soldiers_attend_Finnish_army%27s_cold_weather_training_150110-A-WX507-585.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Finnish and American soldiers train together in arctic conditions in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lapland,_Finland" title="Lapland, Finland">Lapland, Finland</a>, as part of Cold Weather Basic Operation Course, January 6–16, 2015</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_recruit_training" title="Military recruit training">Military recruit training</a></div>
<p>Initial training conditions recruits for the demands of military life, including preparedness to injure and kill other people, and to face mortal danger without fleeing. It is a physically and psychologically intensive process which <a href="/wiki/Resocialization" title="Resocialization">resocializes</a> recruits for the unique nature of military demands. For example:
</p>
<ul><li>Individuality is suppressed (e.g. by shaving the head of new recruits, issuing uniforms, denying privacy, and prohibiting the use of first names);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:22_27-0"><a href="#cite_note-:22-27">[27]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:42_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-:42-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li>Daily routine is tightly controlled (e.g. recruits must make their beds, polish boots, and stack their clothes in a certain way, and mistakes are punished);<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-:6-29">[29]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:42_28-1"><a href="#cite_note-:42-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li>Continuous <a href="/wiki/Stressor" title="Stressor">stressors</a> deplete psychological resistance to the demands of their instructors (e.g. depriving recruits of sleep, food, or shelter, shouting insults and giving orders intended to humiliate)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:32_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-:32-30">[30]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:42_28-2"><a href="#cite_note-:42-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:6_29-1"><a href="#cite_note-:6-29">[29]</a></sup></li>
<li>Frequent punishments serve to condition group conformity and discourage poor performance;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-:42_28-3"><a href="#cite_note-:42-28">[28]</a></sup></li>
<li>The disciplined drill instructor is presented as a role model of the ideal soldier.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup></li></ul>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Intelligence">Intelligence</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_intelligence" title="Military intelligence">Military intelligence</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Military&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2017</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The next requirement comes as a fairly basic need for the military to identify possible <a href="/wiki/Military_threat" title="Military threat">threats</a> it may be called upon to face. For this purpose, some of the commanding forces and other military, as well as often civilian personnel participate in identification of these threats. This is at once an organization, a system and a process collectively called <a href="/wiki/Military_intelligence" title="Military intelligence">military intelligence</a> (MI).
</p><p>The difficulty in using military intelligence concepts and military intelligence methods is in the nature of the <a href="/wiki/Information_security" title="Information security">secrecy</a> of the information they seek, and the <a href="/wiki/Clandestine_operation" title="Clandestine operation">clandestine</a> nature that intelligence operatives work in obtaining what may be plans for a <a href="/wiki/Conflict_escalation" title="Conflict escalation">conflict escalation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phase_(combat)" title="Phase (combat)">initiation of combat</a>, or an <a href="/wiki/Invasion" title="Invasion">invasion</a>.
</p><p>An important part of the military intelligence role is the military analysis performed to assess <a href="/wiki/Military_capability" title="Military capability">military capability</a> of potential future aggressors, and provide combat modelling that helps to understand factors on which comparison of forces can be made. This helps to quantify and qualify such statements as: "<a href="/wiki/People%27s_Liberation_Army" title="People's Liberation Army">China</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_of_India" title="Military of India">India</a> maintain the largest armed forces in the World" or that "the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/U.S._Military" title="U.S. Military">U.S. Military</a> is considered to be the world's strongest".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Simple_guerrilla_organization.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="143" data-file-width="340" decoding="async" height="93" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Simple_guerrilla_organization.svg/220px-Simple_guerrilla_organization.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Simple_guerrilla_organization.svg/330px-Simple_guerrilla_organization.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Simple_guerrilla_organization.svg/440px-Simple_guerrilla_organization.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Simple_guerrilla_organization.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Guerrilla structure</div></div></div>
<p>Although some groups engaged in combat, such as militants or <a href="/wiki/Resistance_movement" title="Resistance movement">resistance movements</a>, refer to themselves using military terminology, notably 'Army' or 'Front', none have had the structure of a national military to justify the reference, and usually have had to rely on support of outside national militaries. They also use these terms to conceal from the MI their true capabilities, and to impress potential ideological recruits.
</p><p>Having military intelligence representatives participate in the execution of the national defence policy is important, because it becomes the first respondent and commentator on the policy expected <a href="/wiki/Strategic_goal_(military)" title="Strategic goal (military)">strategic goal</a>, compared to the realities of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intelligence_(information_gathering)" title="Intelligence (information gathering)">identified threats</a>. When the intelligence reporting is compared to the policy, it becomes possible for the national leadership to consider allocating resources over and above the officers and their subordinates military pay, and the expense of maintaining military facilities and military support services for them.
</p>

</p>
</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Economics_of_defense" title="Economics of defense">Defense economics</a> is the financial and monetary efforts made to resource and sustain militaries, and to finance <a href="/wiki/Military_operation" title="Military operation">military operations</a>, including war.
</p><p>The process of allocating resources is conducted by determining a <a href="/wiki/Military_budget" title="Military budget">military budget</a>, which is administered by a military finance organization within the military. Military procurement is then authorized to purchase or contract provision of goods and services to the military, whether in peacetime at a permanent base, or in a combat zone from local population.
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">
<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 397.33333333333px"><div style="width: 397.33333333333px">
