<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Capability_development">Capability development</span></h3>
<p>Capability development, which is often referred to as the military 'strength', is arguably one of the most complex activities known to humanity; because it requires determining: strategic, operational, and tactical capability requirements to counter the identified threats; strategic, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operational_doctrine" title="Operational doctrine">operational</a>, and tactical doctrines by which the acquired capabilities will be used; identifying concepts, methods, and systems involved in executing the doctrines; creating design specifications for the manufacturers who would produce these in adequate quantity and quality for their use in combat; purchase the concepts, methods, and systems; create a forces structure that would use the concepts, methods, and systems most effectively and efficiently; integrate these concepts, methods, and systems into the force structure by providing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_education" title="Military education">military education</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_training" title="Military training">training</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Military_exercise" title="Military exercise">practice</a> that preferably resembles combat environment of intended use; create <a href="/wiki/Military_logistics" title="Military logistics">military logistics</a> systems to allow continued and uninterrupted performance of <a href="/wiki/Military_organization" title="Military organization">military organizations</a> under combat conditions, including provision of health services to the personnel, and maintenance for the equipment; the services to assist recovery of wounded personnel, and repair of damaged equipment; and finally, post-conflict <a href="/wiki/Demobilization" title="Demobilization">demobilization</a>, and disposal of war stocks surplus to peacetime requirements.
</p><p>Development of <a href="/wiki/Military_doctrine" title="Military doctrine">military doctrine</a> is perhaps the most important of all capability development activities, because it determines how military forces are used in conflicts, the concepts and methods used by the command to employ appropriately military skilled, <a href="/wiki/Soldier" title="Soldier">armed</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_equipment" title="Military equipment">equipped</a> personnel in achievement of the tangible goals and objectives of the <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">war</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_campaign" title="Military campaign">campaign</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battle" title="Battle">battle</a>, engagement, and action.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p.67,_Dupuy_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-p.67,_Dupuy-35">[35]</a></sup> The line between strategy and tactics is not easily blurred, although deciding which is being discussed had sometimes been a matter of personal judgement by some commentators, and military historians. The use of forces at the level of organization between strategic and tactical is called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operational_mobility" title="Operational mobility">operational mobility</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Science">Science</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_technology" title="Military technology">Military technology</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Military&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2017</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>Because most of the concepts and methods used by the military, and many of its systems are not found in commercial branches, much of the material is researched, designed, developed, and offered for inclusion in <a href="/wiki/Arsenal" title="Arsenal">arsenals</a> by <a href="/wiki/Military_science" title="Military science">military science</a> organizations within the overall structure of the military. Military scientists are therefore found<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (January 2022)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> to interact with all Arms and Services of the armed forces, and at all levels of the military hierarchy of command.
</p><p>Although concerned with research into <a href="/wiki/Military_psychology" title="Military psychology">military psychology</a>, particularly <a href="/wiki/Combat_stress_reaction" title="Combat stress reaction">combat stress</a> and how it affect troop <a href="/wiki/Morale" title="Morale">morale</a>, often the bulk of military science activities is directed at military intelligence technology, <a href="/wiki/Military_communications" title="Military communications">military communications</a>, and improving <a href="/wiki/Military_capability" title="Military capability">military capability</a> through research. The design, development, and prototyping of <a href="/wiki/Weapon" title="Weapon">weapons</a>, military support equipment, and <a href="/wiki/Military_technology" title="Military technology">military technology</a> in general, is also an area in which much effort is invested – it includes everything from global communication networks and <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_carrier" title="Aircraft carrier">aircraft carriers</a> to paint and food.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Logistics">Logistics</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_logistics" title="Military logistics">Military logistics</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Military&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2017</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:C-1Transport_aircraft02.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="354" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/C-1Transport_aircraft02.jpg/220px-C-1Transport_aircraft02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/C-1Transport_aircraft02.jpg/330px-C-1Transport_aircraft02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/C-1Transport_aircraft02.jpg/440px-C-1Transport_aircraft02.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:C-1Transport_aircraft02.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Kawasaki_C-1" title="Kawasaki C-1">Kawasaki C-1</a> is a tactical military transport of the <a href="/wiki/Japan_Air_Self-Defense_Force" title="Japan Air Self-Defense Force">Japan Air Self-Defense Force</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Convoy_Red_Ball_Express.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1240" data-file-width="1603" decoding="async" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Convoy_Red_Ball_Express.jpg/220px-Convoy_Red_Ball_Express.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Convoy_Red_Ball_Express.jpg/330px-Convoy_Red_Ball_Express.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Convoy_Red_Ball_Express.jpg/440px-Convoy_Red_Ball_Express.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Convoy_Red_Ball_Express.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Red_Ball_Express" title="Red Ball Express">Red Ball Express</a> convoy in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a></div></div></div>
<p>Possessing military capability is not sufficient if this capability cannot be deployed for, and employed in combat operations. To achieve this, <a href="/wiki/Military_logistics" title="Military logistics">military logistics</a> are used for the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Logistics_management" title="Logistics management">logistics management</a> and logistics planning of the forces <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_supply_chain_management" title="Military supply chain management">military supply chain management</a>, the consumables, and capital equipment of the troops.
</p><p>Although mostly concerned with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_transport" title="Military transport">military transport</a>, as a means of delivery using different modes of transport; from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_truck" title="Military truck">military trucks</a>, to <a href="/wiki/Container_ship" title="Container ship">container ships</a> operating from permanent <a href="/wiki/Military_base" title="Military base">military base</a>, it also involves creating field supply dumps at the rear of the <a href="/wiki/Combat" title="Combat">combat</a> zone, and even forward supply points in specific unit's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tactical_Area_of_Responsibility" title="Tactical Area of Responsibility">Tactical Area of Responsibility</a>.
</p><p>These supply points are also used to provide <a href="/wiki/Military_engineering" title="Military engineering">military engineering</a> services, such as the recovery of defective and derelict vehicles and weapons, maintenance of weapons in the field, the repair and field modification of weapons and equipment; and in peacetime, the life-extension programmes undertaken to allow continued use of equipment. One of the most important role of logistics is the supply of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Munition" title="Munition">munitions</a> as a primary type of consumable, their storage, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ordnance_disposal" title="Ordnance disposal">disposal</a>.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_combat">In combat</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-Unreferenced_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Unreferenced" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>does not <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">cite</a> any <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">sources</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Military&amp;action=edit">improve this section</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability#Burden_of_evidence" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">removed</a>.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2017</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>The primary reason for the existence of the military is to engage in <a href="/wiki/Combat" title="Combat">combat</a>, should it be required to do so by the national defence policy, and to win. This represents an organisational goal of any military, and the primary focus for military thought through <a href="/wiki/Military_history" title="Military history">military history</a>. How <a href="/wiki/Victory" title="Victory">victory</a> is achieved, and what shape it assumes, is studied by most, if not all, military groups on three levels.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Strategic_victory">Strategic victory</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Strategic_victory" title="Strategic victory">Strategic victory</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Military&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2017</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mahratta_pirates_attacking_the_sloop_%27Aurora%27,_of_the_Bombay_Marine,_1812;_end_of_the_action_RMG_BHC1085.tiff"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2887" data-file-width="4867" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Mahratta_pirates_attacking_the_sloop_%27Aurora%27%2C_of_the_Bombay_Marine%2C_1812%3B_end_of_the_action_RMG_BHC1085.tiff/lossy-page1-220px-Mahratta_pirates_attacking_the_sloop_%27Aurora%27%2C_of_the_Bombay_Marine%2C_1812%3B_end_of_the_action_RMG_BHC1085.tiff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Mahratta_pirates_attacking_the_sloop_%27Aurora%27%2C_of_the_Bombay_Marine%2C_1812%3B_end_of_the_action_RMG_BHC1085.tiff/lossy-page1-330px-Mahratta_pirates_attacking_the_sloop_%27Aurora%27%2C_of_the_Bombay_Marine%2C_1812%3B_end_of_the_action_RMG_BHC1085.tiff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Mahratta_pirates_attacking_the_sloop_%27Aurora%27%2C_of_the_Bombay_Marine%2C_1812%3B_end_of_the_action_RMG_BHC1085.tiff/lossy-page1-440px-Mahratta_pirates_attacking_the_sloop_%27Aurora%27%2C_of_the_Bombay_Marine%2C_1812%3B_end_of_the_action_RMG_BHC1085.tiff.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mahratta_pirates_attacking_the_sloop_%27Aurora%27,_of_the_Bombay_Marine,_1812;_end_of_the_action_RMG_BHC1085.tiff" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Maratha_Navy" title="Maratha Navy">Maratha Navy</a>, which is considered to be the foundation of the modern <a href="/wiki/Indian_Navy" title="Indian Navy">Indian Navy</a>, often employed land and sea coordination tactics when attacking, which won them many battles against the <a href="/wiki/Mughal_Empire" title="Mughal Empire">Mughals</a> and <a href="/wiki/Portuguese_Empire" title="Portuguese Empire">Portuguese</a></div></div></div>
<p><a href="/wiki/Military_strategy" title="Military strategy">Military strategy</a> is the management of forces in <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">wars</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_campaign" title="Military campaign">military campaigns</a> by a <a href="/wiki/Commander-in-chief" title="Commander-in-chief">commander-in-chief</a>, employing large military forces, either national and allied as a whole, or the component elements of <a href="/wiki/Army" title="Army">armies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Navy" title="Navy">navies</a> and <a href="/wiki/Air_force" title="Air force">air forces</a>; such as <a href="/wiki/Army_group" title="Army group">army groups</a>, <a href="/wiki/Naval_fleet" title="Naval fleet">naval fleets</a>, and large numbers of <a href="/wiki/Aircraft" title="Aircraft">aircraft</a>. Military strategy is a long-term projection of belligerents' policy, with a broad view of outcome implications, including outside the concerns of military command. Military strategy is more concerned with the <a href="/wiki/Logistics" title="Logistics">supply of war</a> and planning, than management of field forces and combat between them. The scope of strategic military planning can span weeks, but is more often months or even years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p.67,_Dupuy_35-1"><a href="#cite_note-p.67,_Dupuy-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p>
<div style="clear:both;"></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Operational_victory">Operational victory</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Military&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2017</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Crowd_of_Dutch_civilians_celebrating_the_liberation_of_Utrecht_by_the_Canadian_Army.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="490" decoding="async" height="216" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Crowd_of_Dutch_civilians_celebrating_the_liberation_of_Utrecht_by_the_Canadian_Army.jpg/220px-Crowd_of_Dutch_civilians_celebrating_the_liberation_of_Utrecht_by_the_Canadian_Army.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Crowd_of_Dutch_civilians_celebrating_the_liberation_of_Utrecht_by_the_Canadian_Army.jpg/330px-Crowd_of_Dutch_civilians_celebrating_the_liberation_of_Utrecht_by_the_Canadian_Army.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Crowd_of_Dutch_civilians_celebrating_the_liberation_of_Utrecht_by_the_Canadian_Army.jpg/440px-Crowd_of_Dutch_civilians_celebrating_the_liberation_of_Utrecht_by_the_Canadian_Army.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Crowd_of_Dutch_civilians_celebrating_the_liberation_of_Utrecht_by_the_Canadian_Army.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Dutch civilians celebrating the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/I_Canadian_Corps" title="I Canadian Corps">I Canadian Corps</a> in <a href="/wiki/Utrecht" title="Utrecht">Utrecht</a> as the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Army" title="Canadian Army">Canadian Army</a> liberates the Netherlands from Nazi occupation</div></div></div>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operational_mobility" title="Operational mobility">Operational mobility</a> is, within <a href="/wiki/War" title="War">warfare</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_doctrine" title="Military doctrine">military doctrine</a>, the level of command which coordinates the minute details of <a href="/wiki/Military_tactics" title="Military tactics">tactics</a> with the overarching goals of <a href="/wiki/Strategy" title="Strategy">strategy</a>. A common synonym is operational art.
</p><p>The operational level is at a scale bigger than one where line of sight and the time of day are important, and smaller than the strategic level, where production and politics are considerations. Formations are of the operational level if they are able to conduct operations on their own, and are of sufficient size to be directly handled or have a significant impact at the strategic level. This concept was pioneered by the <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">German</a> army prior to and during the <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">Second World War</a>. At this level, planning and duration of activities takes from one week to a month, and are executed by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Field_Army" title="Field Army">Field Armies</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Army_Corps" title="Army Corps">Army Corps</a> and their naval and air equivalents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p.67,_Dupuy_35-2"><a href="#cite_note-p.67,_Dupuy-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tactical_victory">Tactical victory</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Tactical_victory" title="Tactical victory">Tactical victory</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Military&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">March 2017</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<p><a href="/wiki/Military_tactics" title="Military tactics">Military tactics</a> concerns itself with the methods for engaging and defeating the enemy in direct combat. Military tactics are usually used by units over hours or days, and are focused on the specific, close proximity tasks and objectives of <a href="/wiki/Squadron_(army)" title="Squadron (army)">squadrons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Company_(military_unit)" title="Company (military unit)">companies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Battalion" title="Battalion">battalions</a>, <a href="/wiki/Regiment" title="Regiment">regiments</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brigade" title="Brigade">brigades</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Division_(military)" title="Division (military)">divisions</a>, and their naval and air force equivalents.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-p.67,_Dupuy_35-3"><a href="#cite_note-p.67,_Dupuy-35">[35]</a></sup>
</p><p>One of the oldest military publications is <i><a href="/wiki/The_Art_of_War" title="The Art of War">The Art of War</a></i>, by the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Chinese_philosophers" title="List of Chinese philosophers">Chinese philosopher</a> <a href="/wiki/Sun_Tzu" title="Sun Tzu">Sun Tzu</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Written in the 6th century BCE, the 13-chapter book is intended as military instruction, and not as <a href="/wiki/Military_theory" title="Military theory">military theory</a>, but has had a huge influence on Asian military doctrine, and from the late 19th century, on European and United States <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_plan" title="Military plan">military planning</a>. It has even been used to formulate business tactics, and can even be applied in social and political areas.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Naming_conventions_(geographic_names)" title="Wikipedia:Naming conventions (geographic names)"><span title="The geographic scope near this tag is ambiguous. (July 2011)">where?</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Macedonian_battle_formation-en.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="447" data-file-width="734" decoding="async" height="134" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Macedonian_battle_formation-en.svg/220px-Macedonian_battle_formation-en.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Macedonian_battle_formation-en.svg/330px-Macedonian_battle_formation-en.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/Macedonian_battle_formation-en.svg/440px-Macedonian_battle_formation-en.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Macedonian_battle_formation-en.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Battle formation and tactics of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Macedon" title="Macedon">Macedon</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>The Classical Greeks and the Romans wrote prolifically on <a href="/wiki/Military_campaign" title="Military campaign">military campaigning</a>. Among the best-known Roman works are <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">Julius Caesar</a>'s commentaries on the <a href="/wiki/Gallic_Wars" title="Gallic Wars">Gallic Wars</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Caesar%27s_civil_war" title="Caesar's civil war">Roman Civil war</a> – written about 50 BC.
</p><p>Two major works on tactics come from the late Roman period: <i>Taktike Theoria</i> by <a href="/wiki/Aelianus_Tacticus" title="Aelianus Tacticus">Aelianus Tacticus</a>, and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/De_Re_Militari" title="De Re Militari">De Re Militari</a></i> ('On military matters') by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Publius_Flavius_Vegetius_Renatus" title="Publius Flavius Vegetius Renatus">Vegetius</a>. <i>Taktike Theoria</i> examined Greek military tactics, and was most influential in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Byzantine" title="Byzantine">Byzantine</a> world and during the <a href="/wiki/Islamic_Golden_Age" title="Islamic Golden Age">Golden Age of Islam</a>.
</p><p><i>De Re Militari</i> formed the basis of European military tactics until the late 17th century. Perhaps its most enduring maxim is <a href="/wiki/Si_vis_pacem,_para_bellum" title="Si vis pacem, para bellum"><i>Igitur qui desiderat pacem, praeparet bellum</i></a> (let he who desires peace prepare for war).
</p><p>Due to the changing nature of combat with the introduction of <a href="/wiki/Artillery" title="Artillery">artillery</a> in the European <a href="/wiki/Middle_Ages" title="Middle Ages">Middle Ages</a>, and infantry firearms in the <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, attempts were made to define and identify those strategies, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_tactics" title="Grand tactics">grand tactics</a>, and tactics that would produce a victory more often than that achieved by the Romans in praying to the gods before the battle.
</p><p>
Later this became known as <a href="/wiki/Military_science" title="Military science">military science</a>, and later still, would adopt the <a href="/wiki/Scientific_method" title="Scientific method">scientific method</a> approach to the conduct of military operations under the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> thinking. In his seminal book <i><a href="/wiki/On_War" title="On War">On War</a></i>, the <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussian</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Major-General" title="Major-General">Major-General</a> and leading <a href="/wiki/Expert" title="Expert">expert</a> on modern <a href="/wiki/Military_strategy" title="Military strategy">military strategy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Carl_von_Clausewitz" title="Carl von Clausewitz">Carl von Clausewitz</a> defined military strategy as 'the employment of battles to gain the end of war'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> According to Clausewitz: </p><blockquote>
<p>strategy forms the plan of the War, and to this end it links together the series of acts which are to lead to the final decision, that is to say, it makes the plans for the separate campaigns and regulates the combats to be fought in each.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup>
</p>
</blockquote>
<p>Hence, Clausewitz placed political aims above <a href="/wiki/Strategic_goal_(military)" title="Strategic goal (military)">military goals</a>, ensuring <a href="/wiki/Civilian_control_of_the_military" title="Civilian control of the military">civilian control of the military</a>. Military strategy was one of a triumvirate of '<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_art_(Military_science)" title="Military art (Military science)">arts</a>' or 'sciences' that governed the conduct of warfare, the others being: <a href="/wiki/Military_tactics" title="Military tactics">military tactics</a>, the execution of plans and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Operational_mobility" title="Operational mobility">manoeuvring of forces in battle</a>, and maintenance of an army.
</p><p>The meaning of military tactics has changed over time; from the deployment and manoeuvring of entire land armies on the fields of ancient battles, and galley fleets; to modern use of small unit <a href="/wiki/Ambush" title="Ambush">ambushes</a>, <a href="/wiki/Encirclement" title="Encirclement">encirclements</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bombardment" title="Bombardment">bombardment</a> attacks, <a href="/wiki/Frontal_assault" title="Frontal assault">frontal assaults</a>, <a href="/wiki/Air_assault" title="Air assault">air assaults</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hit-and-run_tactics" title="Hit-and-run tactics">hit-and-run tactics</a> used mainly by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Guerrilla" title="Guerrilla">guerrilla</a> forces, and, in some cases, <a href="/wiki/Suicide_attack" title="Suicide attack">suicide attacks</a> on land and at sea. Evolution of <a href="/wiki/Aerial_warfare" title="Aerial warfare">aerial warfare</a> introduced its own <a href="/wiki/Air_combat_manoeuvring" title="Air combat manoeuvring">air combat tactics</a>. Often, <a href="/wiki/Military_deception" title="Military deception">military deception</a>, in the form of <a href="/wiki/Military_camouflage" title="Military camouflage">military camouflage</a> or misdirection using <a href="/wiki/Decoy" title="Decoy">decoys</a>, is used to confuse the enemy as a tactic.
</p><p>A major development in <a href="/wiki/Infantry_tactics" title="Infantry tactics">infantry tactics</a> came with the increased use of <a href="/wiki/Trench_warfare" title="Trench warfare">trench warfare</a> in the 19th and 20th centuries. This was mainly employed in <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Battle_of_Gallipoli" title="Battle of Gallipoli">Gallipoli campaign</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Western_Front_(World_War_I)" title="Western Front (World War I)">Western Front</a>. Trench warfare often turned to a stalemate, only broken by a large loss of life, because, in order to attack an enemy entrenchment, soldiers had to run through an exposed '<a href="/wiki/No_man%27s_land" title="No man's land">no man's land</a>' under heavy fire from their opposing entrenched enemy.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Technology">Technology</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Military_technology" title="Military technology">Military technology</a></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Military&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2014</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arrow-head_Olynthus_BM_GR1912.4-19.4.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="775" data-file-width="2650" decoding="async" height="64" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Arrow-head_Olynthus_BM_GR1912.4-19.4.jpg/220px-Arrow-head_Olynthus_BM_GR1912.4-19.4.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Arrow-head_Olynthus_BM_GR1912.4-19.4.jpg/330px-Arrow-head_Olynthus_BM_GR1912.4-19.4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d8/Arrow-head_Olynthus_BM_GR1912.4-19.4.jpg/440px-Arrow-head_Olynthus_BM_GR1912.4-19.4.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Arrow-head_Olynthus_BM_GR1912.4-19.4.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arrow-head" title="Arrow-head">Arrow-head</a>. Bronze, 4th century BC. From <a href="/wiki/Olynthus" title="Olynthus">Olynthus</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chalcidice" title="Chalcidice">Chalcidice</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>As with any occupation, since the ancient times, the military has been distinguished from other members of the society by their tools, the military weapons, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_equipment" title="Military equipment">military equipment</a> used in combat. When <a href="/wiki/Stone_Age" title="Stone Age">Stone Age</a> humans first took a sliver of flint to tip the <a href="/wiki/Spear" title="Spear">spear</a>, it was the first example of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Applied_research" title="Applied research">applying technology</a> to improve the weapon.
</p><p>Since then, the advances made by human societies, and that of weapons, has been irretrievably linked. Stone weapons gave way to <a href="/wiki/Bronze_Age" title="Bronze Age">Bronze Age</a> weapons, and later, the <a href="/wiki/Iron_Age" title="Iron Age">Iron Age</a> weapons. With each technological change, was realized some tangible increase in military capability, such as through greater effectiveness of a sharper edge in defeating <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leather_armour" title="Leather armour">leather armour</a>, or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mechanics_of_materials" title="Mechanics of materials">improved density of materials</a> used in manufacture of weapons.
</p><p>On <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Land_warfare" title="Land warfare">land</a>, the first really significant technological advance in warfare was the development of the <a href="/wiki/Ranged_weapon" title="Ranged weapon">ranged weapons</a>, and notably, the <a href="/wiki/Sling_(weapon)" title="Sling (weapon)">sling</a>. The next significant advance came with the <a href="/wiki/Domestication_of_the_horse" title="Domestication of the horse">domestication of the horses</a> and mastering of <a href="/wiki/Equestrianism" title="Equestrianism">equestrianism</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Armor_for_Man_and_Horse,_Italy_(probably_Milan),_c._1565,_and_Field_armor_for_horseman,_Italy,_c._1575_-_Nelson-Atkins_Museum_of_Art_-_DSC08601.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3240" data-file-width="4320" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Armor_for_Man_and_Horse%2C_Italy_%28probably_Milan%29%2C_c._1565%2C_and_Field_armor_for_horseman%2C_Italy%2C_c._1575_-_Nelson-Atkins_Museum_of_Art_-_DSC08601.JPG/220px-Armor_for_Man_and_Horse%2C_Italy_%28probably_Milan%29%2C_c._1565%2C_and_Field_armor_for_horseman%2C_Italy%2C_c._1575_-_Nelson-Atkins_Museum_of_Art_-_DSC08601.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Armor_for_Man_and_Horse%2C_Italy_%28probably_Milan%29%2C_c._1565%2C_and_Field_armor_for_horseman%2C_Italy%2C_c._1575_-_Nelson-Atkins_Museum_of_Art_-_DSC08601.JPG/330px-Armor_for_Man_and_Horse%2C_Italy_%28probably_Milan%29%2C_c._1565%2C_and_Field_armor_for_horseman%2C_Italy%2C_c._1575_-_Nelson-Atkins_Museum_of_Art_-_DSC08601.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Armor_for_Man_and_Horse%2C_Italy_%28probably_Milan%29%2C_c._1565%2C_and_Field_armor_for_horseman%2C_Italy%2C_c._1575_-_Nelson-Atkins_Museum_of_Art_-_DSC08601.JPG/440px-Armor_for_Man_and_Horse%2C_Italy_%28probably_Milan%29%2C_c._1565%2C_and_Field_armor_for_horseman%2C_Italy%2C_c._1575_-_Nelson-Atkins_Museum_of_Art_-_DSC08601.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Armor_for_Man_and_Horse,_Italy_(probably_Milan),_c._1565,_and_Field_armor_for_horseman,_Italy,_c._1575_-_Nelson-Atkins_Museum_of_Art_-_DSC08601.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mounted and foot <a href="/wiki/Armour" title="Armour">armoured</a> <a href="/wiki/Knight" title="Knight">knights</a>. Armour and <a href="/wiki/Cavalry" title="Cavalry">cavalry</a> dominated the battlefield, until the invention of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Firearms" title="Firearms">firearms</a>.</div></div></div>
<p>Arguably, the greatest invention that affected not just the military, but all society, after adoption of fire, was the <a href="/wiki/Wheel" title="Wheel">wheel</a>, and its use in the construction of the <a href="/wiki/Chariot" title="Chariot">chariot</a>. There were no advances in military technology, until, from the mechanical arm action of a slinger, the <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greece" title="Ancient Greece">Greeks</a>, <a href="/wiki/Egyptians" title="Egyptians">Egyptians</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Empire" title="Roman Empire">Romans</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Persia" title="Persia">Persians</a>, <a href="/wiki/History_of_China#Ancient_China" title="History of China">Chinese</a>, etc., developed the <a href="/wiki/Siege_engine" title="Siege engine">siege engines</a>. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bow_(weapon)" title="Bow (weapon)">bow</a> was manufactured in increasingly larger and more powerful versions, to increase both the weapon range, and armour penetration performance. These developed into the powerful composite and recurve bows, and crossbows of <a href="/wiki/History_of_China#Ancient_China" title="History of China">Ancient China</a>. These proved particularly useful during the rise of cavalry, as horsemen encased in ever-more sophisticated <a href="/wiki/Armour" title="Armour">armour</a> came to dominate the battlefield.
</p><p>Somewhat earlier, in medieval China, <a href="/wiki/Gunpowder" title="Gunpowder">gunpowder</a> had been invented, and was increasingly used by the military in combat. The use of gunpowder in the early <a href="/wiki/Mortar_(weapon)" title="Mortar (weapon)">vase-like mortars</a> in Europe, and advanced versions of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Long_bow" title="Long bow">long bow</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cross_bow" title="Cross bow">cross bow</a>, which all had armour-piercing <a href="/wiki/Arrowhead" title="Arrowhead">arrowheads</a>, that put an end to the dominance of the armoured knight. After the long bow, which required great skill and strength to use, the next most significant technological advance was the <a href="/wiki/Musket" title="Musket">musket</a>, which could be used effectively, with little training. In time, the successors to muskets and <a href="/wiki/Cannon" title="Cannon">cannon</a>, in the form of <a href="/wiki/Rifle" title="Rifle">rifles</a> and <a href="/wiki/Artillery" title="Artillery">artillery</a>, would become core battlefield technology.
</p><p>As the speed of technological advances accelerated in civilian applications, so too warfare became more <a href="/wiki/Industrial_warfare" title="Industrial warfare">industrialized</a>. The newly invented <a href="/wiki/Machine_gun" title="Machine gun">machine gun</a> and <a href="/wiki/Repeating_rifle" title="Repeating rifle">repeating rifle</a> redefined <a href="/wiki/Firepower" title="Firepower">firepower</a> on the battlefield, and, in part, explains the high casualty rates of the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a>. The next breakthrough was the conversion of artillery parks from the <a href="/wiki/Muzzleloader" title="Muzzleloader">muzzle loading guns</a>, to the quicker loading <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Breech-loading_weapon" title="Breech-loading weapon">breech loading guns</a> with recoiling barrel that allowed quicker aimed fire and use of a shield. The widespread introduction of low smoke (smokeless) propellant powders since the 1880s also allowed for a great improvement of artillery ranges.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:BattleOfVirginiaCapes.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3115" data-file-width="4963" decoding="async" height="138" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/BattleOfVirginiaCapes.jpg/220px-BattleOfVirginiaCapes.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/BattleOfVirginiaCapes.jpg/330px-BattleOfVirginiaCapes.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/BattleOfVirginiaCapes.jpg/440px-BattleOfVirginiaCapes.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:BattleOfVirginiaCapes.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Naval military forces of France and Britain exchange fire at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Chesapeake" title="Battle of the Chesapeake">Battle of the Chesapeake</a></div></div></div>
<p>The development of breech loading had the greatest effect on <a href="/wiki/Naval_warfare" title="Naval warfare">naval warfare</a>, for the first time since the Middle Ages, altering the way weapons are mounted on <a href="/wiki/Warship" title="Warship">warships</a>, and therefore <a href="/wiki/Naval_tactics" title="Naval tactics">naval tactics</a>, now divorced from the reliance on <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Sail" title="Age of Sail">sails</a> with the invention of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Internal_combustion" title="Internal combustion">internal combustion</a>. A further advance in military naval technology was the design of the <a href="/wiki/Submarine" title="Submarine">submarine</a>, and its weapon, the <a href="/wiki/Torpedo" title="Torpedo">torpedo</a>.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Main_battle_tank" title="Main battle tank">Main battle tanks</a>, and other heavy equipment such as <a href="/wiki/Armoured_fighting_vehicle" title="Armoured fighting vehicle">armoured fighting vehicles</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_aircraft" title="Military aircraft">military aircraft</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ship" title="Ship">ships</a>, are characteristic to organized military forces.
</p><p>During <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the need to break the deadlock of trench warfare saw the rapid development of many new technologies, particularly <a href="/wiki/Tank" title="Tank">tanks</a>. <a href="/wiki/Military_aviation" title="Military aviation">Military aviation</a> was extensively used, and <a href="/wiki/Bomber" title="Bomber">bombers</a> became decisive in many battles of <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, which marked the most frantic period of weapons development in history. Many new designs, and concepts were used in combat, and all existing technologies of warfare were improved between 1939 and 1945.
</p><p>During the war, significant advances were made in <a href="/wiki/Military_communications" title="Military communications">military communications</a> through increased use of radio, military intelligence through use of the <a href="/wiki/Radar" title="Radar">radar</a>, and in <a href="/wiki/Military_medicine" title="Military medicine">military medicine</a> through use of <a href="/wiki/Penicillin" title="Penicillin">penicillin</a>, while in the air, the guided <a href="/wiki/Missile" title="Missile">missile</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jet_aircraft" title="Jet aircraft">jet aircraft</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Helicopter" title="Helicopter">helicopters</a> were seen for the first time. Perhaps the most infamous of all military technologies was the creation of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atomic_bomb" title="Atomic bomb">atomic bomb</a>, although the exact effects of its <a href="/wiki/Radiation" title="Radiation">radiation</a> were unknown until the early 1950s. Far greater use of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_vehicles" title="Military vehicles">military vehicles</a> had finally eliminated the cavalry from the military <a href="/wiki/Force_structure" title="Force structure">force structure</a>.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:USAF_F-15C_fires_AIM-7_Sparrow.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1334" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="143" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/USAF_F-15C_fires_AIM-7_Sparrow.jpg/220px-USAF_F-15C_fires_AIM-7_Sparrow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/USAF_F-15C_fires_AIM-7_Sparrow.jpg/330px-USAF_F-15C_fires_AIM-7_Sparrow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/USAF_F-15C_fires_AIM-7_Sparrow.jpg/440px-USAF_F-15C_fires_AIM-7_Sparrow.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:USAF_F-15C_fires_AIM-7_Sparrow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/AIM-7" title="AIM-7">AIM-7</a> Sparrow medium range <a href="/wiki/Air-to-air_missile" title="Air-to-air missile">air-to-air missile</a> from an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-15_Eagle" title="F-15 Eagle">F-15 Eagle</a></div></div></div>
<p>After World War II, with the onset of the <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, the constant technological development of new weapons was institutionalized, as participants engaged in a constant '<a href="/wiki/Arms_race" title="Arms race">arms race</a>' in capability development. This constant state of weapons development continues into the present, and remains a constant drain on national resources, which some<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too-vague attribution or weasel words. (March 2017)">who?</span></a></i>]</sup> blame on the <a href="/wiki/Military%E2%80%93industrial_complex" title="Military–industrial complex">military–industrial complex</a>.
</p><p>The most significant technological developments that influenced combat have been the guided missiles, which can be used by all branches of the armed services. More recently, <a href="/wiki/Information_technology" title="Information technology">information technology</a>, and its use in <a href="/wiki/Surveillance" title="Surveillance">surveillance</a>, including space-based reconnaissance systems, have played an increasing role in military operations.
</p><p>The impact of <a href="/wiki/Information_warfare" title="Information warfare">information warfare</a> that focuses on attacking command communication systems, and military databases, has been coupled with the new development in military technology, has been the use of robotic systems in intelligence combat, both in hardware and software applications.
</p><p>Recently, there has also been a particular focus towards the use of <a href="/wiki/Renewable_fuels" title="Renewable fuels">renewable fuels</a> for running military vehicles on. Unlike fossil fuels, renewable fuels can be produced in any country, creating a strategic advantage. The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/US_military" title="US military">US military</a> has committed itself to have 50% of its energy consumption come from alternative sources.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="As_part_of_society">As part of society</span></h2>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1097763485" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><table class="box-More_citations_needed_section plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div class="mbox-image-div"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg"><img alt="" data-file-height="399" data-file-width="512" decoding="async" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Military&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Referencing_for_beginners" title="Help:Referencing for beginners">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span> <span class="date-container"><i>(<span class="date">October 2014</span>)</i></span><span class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<small><a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a></small>)</i></span></div></td></tr></tbody></table>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Samurai_and_Ainu_Fuzoku_Ema.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1728" data-file-width="2773" decoding="async" height="137" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Samurai_and_Ainu_Fuzoku_Ema.jpg/220px-Samurai_and_Ainu_Fuzoku_Ema.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Samurai_and_Ainu_Fuzoku_Ema.jpg/330px-Samurai_and_Ainu_Fuzoku_Ema.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Samurai_and_Ainu_Fuzoku_Ema.jpg/440px-Samurai_and_Ainu_Fuzoku_Ema.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Samurai_and_Ainu_Fuzoku_Ema.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Samurai" title="Samurai">Samurai</a>, member of the Japanese warrior caste</div></div></div>
<p>For much of <a href="/wiki/Military_history" title="Military history">military history</a>, the armed forces were considered to be for use by the heads of their societies, until recently, the crowned heads of states. In a democracy or other political system run in the public interest, it is a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_force" title="Public force">public force</a>.
</p><p>The relationship between the military and the <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">society</a> it serves is a complicated and ever-evolving one. Much depends on the nature of the society itself, and whether it sees the military as important, as for example in time of threat or war, or a burdensome expense typified by defence cuts in time of peace.
</p><p>One difficult matter in the relation between military and society is control and transparency. In some countries, limited information on military operations and budgeting is accessible for the public. However transparency in the military sector is crucial to fight <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a>. This showed the Government Defence Anti-corruption Index <a href="/wiki/Transparency_International" title="Transparency International">Transparency International UK</a> published in 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup>
</p><p>Militaries often function as <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">societies</a> within societies, by having their own military communities, <a href="/wiki/Military%E2%80%93industrial_complex" title="Military–industrial complex">economies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_education_and_training" title="Military education and training">education</a>, <a href="/wiki/Military_medicine" title="Military medicine">medicine</a>, and other aspects of a functioning <a href="/wiki/Civil_society" title="Civil society">civilian society</a>. Although a 'military' is not limited to nations in of itself as many <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Private_military_companies" title="Private military companies">private military companies</a> (or PMC's) can be used or 'hired' by organizations and figures as security, escort, or other means of protection; where police, agencies, or militaries are absent or not trusted.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ideology_and_ethics">Ideology and ethics</span></h3>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Militarism" title="Militarism">Militarism</a></div>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gustavus_Adolphus_in_action_(probably_at_L%C3%BCtzen).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="506" data-file-width="736" decoding="async" height="151" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Gustavus_Adolphus_in_action_%28probably_at_L%C3%BCtzen%29.jpg/220px-Gustavus_Adolphus_in_action_%28probably_at_L%C3%BCtzen%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Gustavus_Adolphus_in_action_%28probably_at_L%C3%BCtzen%29.jpg/330px-Gustavus_Adolphus_in_action_%28probably_at_L%C3%BCtzen%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/Gustavus_Adolphus_in_action_%28probably_at_L%C3%BCtzen%29.jpg/440px-Gustavus_Adolphus_in_action_%28probably_at_L%C3%BCtzen%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gustavus_Adolphus_in_action_(probably_at_L%C3%BCtzen).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Swedish king <a href="/wiki/Gustavus_Adolphus" title="Gustavus Adolphus">Gustavus Adolphus</a> leading a cavalry charge, 1634</div></div></div>
<p>Militarist ideology is the <a href="/wiki/Society" title="Society">society</a>'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Social_attitude" title="Social attitude">social attitude</a> of being best served, or being a beneficiary of a <a href="/wiki/Government" title="Government">government</a>, or guided by concepts embodied in the military <i>culture, doctrine, system</i>, or <i>leaders</i>.
</p><p>Either because of the <a href="/wiki/Cultural_memory" title="Cultural memory">cultural memory</a>, national history, or the potentiality of a <a href="/wiki/Military_threat" title="Military threat">military threat</a>, the militarist argument asserts that a <a href="/wiki/Civilian" title="Civilian">civilian</a> population is dependent upon, and thereby subservient to the needs and goals of its military for continued <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a>. <a href="/wiki/Militarism" title="Militarism">Militarism</a> is sometimes contrasted with the concepts of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comprehensive_national_power" title="Comprehensive national power">comprehensive national power</a>, <a href="/wiki/Soft_power" title="Soft power">soft power</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hard_power" title="Hard power">hard power</a>.
</p><p>Most nations have separate <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Military_law" title="Military law">military laws</a> which regulate conduct in war and during peacetime. An early exponent was <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Grotius" title="Hugo Grotius">Hugo Grotius</a>, whose <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure_belli_ac_pacis" title="De jure belli ac pacis">On the Law of War and Peace</a></i> (1625) had a major impact of the humanitarian approach to warfare development. His theme was echoed by <a href="/wiki/Gustavus_Adolphus" title="Gustavus Adolphus">Gustavus Adolphus</a>.
</p><p>Ethics of warfare have developed since 1945, to create constraints on the military treatment of prisoners and civilians, primarily by the <a href="/wiki/Geneva_Conventions" title="Geneva Conventions">Geneva Conventions</a>; but rarely apply to use of the military forces as internal security troops during times of political conflict that results in popular protests and incitement to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Popular_uprising" title="Popular uprising">popular uprising</a>.
</p><p>International protocols restrict the use, or have even created international bans on some types of weapons, notably <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Weapons_of_mass_destruction" title="Weapons of mass destruction">weapons of mass destruction</a> (WMD). <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_convention" title="International convention">International conventions</a> define what constitutes a <a href="/wiki/War_crime" title="War crime">war crime</a>, and provides for war crimes prosecution. Individual countries also have elaborate codes of <a href="/wiki/Military_justice" title="Military justice">military justice</a>, an example being the United States' <a href="/wiki/Uniform_Code_of_Military_Justice" title="Uniform Code of Military Justice">Uniform Code of Military Justice</a> that can lead to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Court_martial" title="Court martial">court martial</a> for military personnel found guilty of war crimes.
</p><p>Military actions are sometimes argued to be justified by furthering a humanitarian cause, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Disaster_relief" title="Disaster relief">disaster relief</a> operations, or in defence of refugees. The term <a href="/wiki/Military_humanism" title="Military humanism">military humanism</a> is used to refer to such actions.
</p>
